<gmapID>0x808fb0ee5ca836d7:0xbfaf6bd9414bedf3<//gmapID>< Text>
Good Italian restaurant, been going there for several years. It is located in downtown Los Altos, so you could go there after waking around downtown. Their roasted sun dried tomato based dip that they serve with the bread is awesome. The entrees are largely the typical Italian stuff pastas, some steak, etc. I like their arabbiata sauce, I usually ask them to substitute the marinara with that. The place is small and cozy, usually crowded around 7-8:30 even considering the overflow room they have to the side. In summer you can sit outside, gives you a feel of sitting in a restaurant in Italy. Highly recommend!<//Text>

<date>1578138983769<//date><review>I don't frequent downtown Los Altos nor do I eat Italian often, but I'm glad I tried Pompeii. It's one of those fancier restaurants that one would assume is expensive but actually offer reasonable deals on food given the portions and quality (it's also hard not to fill up on the complimentary bread and olive oil and/or butter at the beginning of the meal). For example, I got the personal size margherita pizza, which amounted to six slices or two servings of very cheesy pizza for $13. The pizza crust was a good chewiness and very hot when they brought it out, which I appreciated. The restaurant is in a corner unit and has big windows that wrap around all the walls, so I can imagine it'd offer prime people watching in the day time. Pleasant!</review>< pictures>
None< /pictures>

< Review>
This is a cute restaurant.  The servers were very nice.  I ordered the tortellini, which was good, though I don't think it's worth nearly $17.  There was complementary bread and dipping sauce.  The sauce was some sort of eggplant-garlic oil.  It was alright.  I definitely would have preferred normal oil and balsamic vinegar, or just butter.  Overall, it was good.  I'm not yearning to visit for a while.</Review>

< review>
Pompeii is a nice little Italian place in downtown Los Altos with a casual but slightly upscale small town feel. I typically order the chicken parmesan, which is good (though not great). The service is always friendly and the prices are reasonable, so my wife and go back occasionally with friends since it's close to our home. You can find a couple places with better Italian food in the south bay, but Pompeii is amongst the best.</review>

<name>Jacqueline Deely</name><time>1522008125328< /time><rate>3<//rate>< Review>
I rarely write reviews but my experience yesterday evening led me to write one.  My friend and I arrived around 7:00pm and were easily seated.  Food was really wonderful, salad and pizza along with my wine selection "Rutherford Sauvignon Blanc". The issue ended up being our waiter.  Initially he was friendly and our food came out very quickly, but as time passed by, we got the impression he wanted us to finish up quickly and get out of there. He brought the dessert menu and stopped by about five times to check if we wanted something. It became a little annoying and I told him I would wave him down when we wanted something. His response was he now had a large table to take care of, so basically "good luck with that!"  Hmmm...so we decided to not bother with dessert since it was going to be an issue for him and we put our credit cards on the table as a sign we were ready to pay the bill.  He passed by a couple of times and since we were not in a rush, did not initially mind. After a few minutes I then decided to give him the "pay the bill" signal as he passed by and he quickly stopped and said "I don't have time for that"!  What?  You don't have time?  How rude is that?  So I said to my friend, okay, he doesn't want to take our money, so I guess we will just leave!  We proceeded to put our credit cards away and our coats on and it was then he stopped with the bill. We paid and left. I was really annoyed that we were made to feel that we were a bother. Our dining experience should not have been impacted or altered because of other people this waiter needed to attend to. For this reason alone I will be reluctant to return. Shame as the food and the ambience of this restaurant was really nice.<//Review>

< Text>
The staff at this shop are absolutely the sweetest! I come back to this location for that reason alone. The coffee is good black, but if you can try one of their suggested specials I would recommend it. I have never had a bad one yet. Their blended drinks are more to my liking in that they taste fresher and less syrupy than Dutch Bros, Dunkin, and Java. They just aren't as over poweringly sweet and I appreciate that. I recommend their mocha. The chunky monkey (If I have the name correct) with coffee in it is my favorite blended drink thus far. They also have had amazing gluten free brownies offered here, so nice of them to have that option. The Kids choices are also awesome. I would highly recommend this drive thru coffee shop!<//Text>

Free and not busy, but also not great. Almost all of the water is drained and will be until 2022 they say. But beyond that, it doesn't feel like a Japanese garden - a few Japanese elements are scattered among a lot of normal California park plants. The Japanese garden in San Mateo, although smaller, is significantly better.<//review>

<Rating>3< /Rating>< Text>
Upon arrival at the Japanese Friendship Garden I quickly realized that there is little to be friends with aside from the concrete. All the pools are drained and devoid of koi. One can only pray that they are still alive... Somewhere. In solidarity I lay my body prone on the gravel floor of the ponds where they once swam so freely. Good plants and vegetation though, I got a few good tree hugs in. It's also fun to gallop on all fours down the dry ravines where the fish and water lilies once fliurished.<//Text>

<Review>This was once one of my favorite places to visit in San Jose. At one time I would even argue that this was a better place to visit than the one in SF. At this point though it's not really worth even stopping at. Two thirds of the ponds have been dry for years. Yes, I understand this was a result of the sewage flood thanks to San Jose not being able to handle a little rain. I also understand this area wastes money on plenty of things that aren't as important to me, and we are talking several years now.

As bad as all that is, today was the final straw  At some point they taped a sign over their hours to close at 4PM. We didn't realize it until the ranger locked my girlfriend and I in. Some shouted, be we weren't able to understand exactly what was said.  We started walking to the gate to see what was going on, instead we only found it locked. In our escape planning we ran into another couple that was trapped as well.  I guess luckily for all of us the fence is in a similar state of disrepair to the ponds since we were a le to find a bald spot in the barbed wire to make a break for it.</Review><response>None< /response>< name>

Beautiful area yet 2/3 koi ponds have been out of service and empty since a 2017 flood killed the pumps and according to posted signage, there is no timeline to fix the ponds. It's a shame a beautiful place like this can't get ANY corporate donors from the numerous companies in the area (some of whom have plenty to give away!) to help fix up the ponds and support maintenance costs.< /text>

<GmapID>0x808e332c3c96029f:0x9963851067f38f63</GmapID>< Review>
This park is incredibly beautiful despite visiting it during construction and during drought. We walked the park for about 30-40 minutes I believe in the spring heat and enjoyed it very much. We saw a lot of koi fishes swimming in one pond and to my personal surprise they had provided shade using smaller tents - taking care of the animals, big plus! It feels very peaceful and calming to walk this park and enjoy the beauty. As a foreigner I enjoyed this a lot because I had never been to the US before and felt like I was in another country, inside of the US. It was rather magical. I believe the park is truly beautiful during it's peak with the water and the fish swimming around, and I hope to return one day. My only complaint is the lack of water, which might have been stated somewhere, but I am not completely sure.< /Review>

<username>Susan Aoki<//username><Date>1568788002423</Date>< Rate>
5</Rate>
< review>
Beautiful and serene.  A gift from the city of Okayama in Japan during the early 60s.   A rare gem in San Jose, 6.5 acres and you will be transported to a thoughtful place where you are encouraged to be in the moment and relax.  Although the City is repairing the ponds from the flood 2.5 years ago still, the garden is still a haven for animals and beauty.  No fee to enter, parking is about $6 in Senter/Alma lot, and $10 in the lot next to Happy Hollow, free parking if you drive around the stadium area if it's not crowded.  Hours are generally 10am to 5pm, but maybe later - check the website.< /review>

<Rating>5<//Rating><Text>This Japanese Garden is in Kelly Park San Jose. Park is around 6 acres, established in 1965` Entrance to the park is free. However there is a $10 fee for parking. You can also find free street parking near by. Great location for photo shoots or just relax in the garden. Garden has three ponds. Pond under the bridge is Koi pond.

This garden got affected by flood in San Jose, couple of years ago. Now restoration is going on in the garden specially Koi pond. Now the Koi pond is dry, Koi fish are moved to another pond in the garden. Now fund raising in progress to restore the garden.

In spite of this it is still a nice place to visit in San Jose.<//Text>< pics>
